Zhang Mengzhou's Good Times Don't Last Long: Two Concubines Flee Simultaneously

The youngest concubine, Shang Si, is asked to return, and the court reschedules the hearing.

Nanjing: Zhang Mengzhou, a clerk in Nanjing and a native of Sheng County, is forty-eight years old. His original wife, Cao, has borne him a son and two daughters, all over ten years old. However, Zhang, being a long-time resident in Shanghai, felt his life was rather dull. He then made every effort to find beautiful women to amuse himself. Through the efforts of pimps and matchmakers, he began cohabiting with Lin Cuiying, a woman from Xiangshan, in February of this year. Zhang was well aware that current laws do not allow concubinage, so although he had Lin to share his bed, he never gave her a formal title. Unexpectedly, after more than a month of cohabitation, Zhang suddenly became more ambitious and took in Pan Xiaofeng, also from Xiangshan, to fulfill his wish of having women on both sides. Miss Pan was in her prime, with a plump figure, still retaining her rustic charm. After joining Zhang's household, she and Lin were ranked as sisters, with Lin being the elder sister and Pan the younger. They got along quite well, and initially, they knew how to be good wives to Zhang. All of Zhang's friends envied him for having such good luck in his middle age, managing to achieve such a feat with one arrow. Unexpectedly, Zhang was unable to enjoy this kind of romantic life for long. On the morning of the 21st of last month, while Zhang was away at the pharmacy, the two women suddenly fled together, taking all the belongings in the residence. Upon receiving a phone call from the landlord, he rushed back to his residence at No. 3, Lane 1405, Rue Edouard VII, only to find that the women had disappeared. He immediately started investigating and learned the whole story of the two women's escape. It turned out that there was a third party directing things behind the scenes. However, he was worried that publicizing the matter would escalate the incident, and it would not only affect his reputation. But unwilling to let his belongings be sacrificed, he reported to the police station, requesting an investigation. At the same time, he hired lawyers Fan Gang and Fan Qisheng to file a lawsuit in the First Special District Court, requesting that the two women be ordered to return to cohabitation and return the property. He claimed that at the beginning of their cohabitation, the two women were harmonious, but in the past month or two, their temperament had suddenly changed. They put on makeup and went out for fun. When he tried to persuade them, they retorted. On the 21st of last month, they suddenly took their clothes and belongings, loaded them onto four rickshaws, and fled together. Later, they even sent a letter through lawyer Wang, falsely claiming that the plaintiff had abandoned them, but they did not mention the items they had taken. The plaintiff believed that their actions were entirely influenced by others, so he sent a letter back, informing them to return home immediately and bring back the items, promising not to pursue the matter. Who knew that they ignored him, so he had to sue, and so on. Yesterday afternoon, Judge Peng Shi opened the court to summon the two defendants. Only Pan Xiaofeng arrived. Zhang Mengzhou recounted the process of taking the two concubines and presented two documents signed by the families of Pan and Lin as evidence. Then, he claimed that his original wife in his hometown already knew about the concubinage and that he had decided to give all his family property in his hometown to his wife and children, while the living expenses of the two concubines would be provided by his income in Shanghai, and so on. Questioned, the defendant Pan Xiaofeng testified that Zhu Yuying was the matchmaker, and negotiations began in December of last year. Zhu brought one hundred yuan and said that Zhang was marrying a substitute wife. On the fifth day of the first lunar month of this year, she went to Shanghai from her hometown with Zhu and her uncle and met Zhang in the inn. The next day, Zhu said that Zhang did not like her, and the matter was not successful. She returned to Xiangshan. On the seventh day of the first month, she was summoned by Zhang's letter, so she went to Shanghai again with her mother and uncle. Her aunt then signed the note in the hotel, and from then on, she became Zhang's concubine. Recently, Lin Cuiying repeatedly said that Zhang was going to sell her, so she ordered them to flee together, and she was deceived by her. She is now willing to follow Zhang. All her clothes and belongings were taken away by Lin. Lin is now at her cousin's place at 1765 next to the China Hotel on Guizhou Road, and she is staying at a relative's house of Zhu Yuying at Dadongmen, and so on. Judge Peng then instructed to reschedule the hearing and summon Lin Cuiying to court for further questioning. After the court adjourned, Pan Xiaofeng, lacking living expenses, wanted to return with Zhang immediately, but Zhang, with the lawsuit unresolved, not only did not immediately take her in but took out eight small coins and gave them to her.

Taxpayers Association Asks the Municipal Council to Stop the Police from Inspecting Goods Entering and Exiting Warehouses

The Chinese Taxpayers Association of the Public Concession sent a letter to the Municipal Council yesterday, which stated: "We are writing to inform you that, according to a letter from Renyuhao, our company has been operating a Ningbo Hengfeng Factory cloth business at No. 3, Ruixingfang, North Wuxi Road, for many years. We rent a warehouse at No. 333, Hainning Road, North Fujian Road. Every day, goods entering and exiting the warehouse are inspected and fined by the police. Last year, we wrote to your council asking for assistance in resolving this matter, but unexpectedly, the police have suddenly resumed inspecting our warehouse. We are not sure why. Moreover, this warehouse area is located in a quiet area with a fixed flow of goods entering and exiting, and it does not obstruct the traffic of passersby in any way. Our limited scope of business is already suffering from the economic downturn. Any inspection would cause great alarm and distress. Therefore, we are writing to ask your council to help alleviate the hardship of businesses and instruct the police department to find a way to prevent future inspections, for which we would be eternally grateful." The letter stated that the warehousing of goods in Shanghai is a necessary practice for commerce. Without this practice, there would be no commerce, and no business, public or private, could operate. Reading the letter, every line is filled with fear and despair, making one feel that it is not easy to be a businessman. The French Municipal Council Denies Collecting Garbage Fees

This issue of the French Concession Municipal Council's weekly municipal report denies the rumor that residents will have to pay extra for garbage disposal. It states that the garbage disposal regulations issued by the French Consulate in July 1932 have not been changed in any way. The garbage on the roads within the concession is cleaned up by the coolies dispatched by the Municipal Council, and no fees are charged. However, residents in the alleys who need the Municipal Council to clean up their garbage must pay 4% of the house tax every six months. It is reported that the Municipal Council's denial is because the Russian-language "Daily News" recently published a statement that the Municipal Council would collect garbage fees. The newspaper believed that the Municipal Council prohibited the sale of ten days in the concession.

Request to Stop the Armed Drills of Railway Police at the North Station: Petitions from the Two Railway Party Headquarters and One District Branch

The railway police under the jurisdiction of the Jinghu and Huhangyong Railway Police Department have recently been conducting armed drills in front of and behind the North Station Garden and on the North Station platform every day. The First District Branch of the Railway Party Headquarters believes that this is detrimental to traffic order and obstructs passengers. They have specially petitioned to request a stop. The original petition is extracted as follows: "Petition requesting that the Special Party Headquarters be forwarded to the Railway Bureau, ordering the Police Department not to send police to conduct drills at the North Station, in order to reassure travelers. On the 19th of this month, the Police Department staff led forty to fifty railway police officers in full armed gear, conducting drills on the North Station Garden outside the fence and on the platform inside the station. They shouted commands, creating a tense situation. Spectators gathered, and the arriving and departing passengers were shocked to see a large group of police officers. The staff of various agencies near the North Station frequently heard loud shouts, and their moods were disrupted. The North Station is the main station for the two railways, with tens of thousands of passengers arriving and departing every day. There are many vehicles, and it is often crowded. When the railway police conduct drills here, if people give way to the vehicles, the police team will not be in formation, and if the vehicles give way to the people, traffic will be obstructed. The police department has training grounds in Jiangwan, Tiantong'an, and the McGuinness Road car repair field, but they do not use them. They uniquely use the North Station, where traffic is congested, as a training ground. Their intention is difficult to understand. At a time when business is slow and rumors are rampant, this kind of action seems inappropriate. The 11th First Executive Committee meeting of this branch decided to petition for a letter to be forwarded to the Railway Bureau, ordering the Police Department not to send police to conduct drills at the North Station, in order to reassure people and maintain traffic. This document is respectfully submitted, and we hope that it will be forwarded to the Railway Bureau, ordering the Police Department not to send police to conduct drills at the North Station, in order to reassure people and maintain traffic."

The defendant was still in prison. When he left the court, the lights of thousands of families were already on.

Introduction to the New Book "Bamboo Papermaking"

"Bamboo Papermaking," written by Luo Ji of Yuzhang in twenty chapters, elaborates in detail and clearly on the types of bamboo, the evolution of bamboo, the standards for bamboo raw materials and manufacturing methods, the standard steaming method, the standard charging method, bleaching method, oiling method, chrysanthemum glue, reference to rice straw, etc. It is indeed a work of cultural merit. The original book is printed on jade paper made according to the method in the book. I received a complimentary copy yesterday and write this note of thanks and introduction.

Special Item: Opinions on the Issue of Increasing Credit Instruments

Four. Deformities in the Long-Term Capital Market's Credit Instruments: There are deformities in the long-term capital market. First, the predominance of foreign commercial securities; second, the imbalanced development of fiscal securities in the Chinese commercial securities market; and third, the high liquidity of real estate deeds. In short, the current long-term capital market is by no means an industrial and commercial long-term capital market under the Chinese national economic system. Please elaborate:

Before the silver crisis, foreign-owned public companies, with the assistance of foreign banks, actively bought and sold foreign commercial securities in China. There were as many as one hundred and several dozen types of listed stocks and corporate bonds. Prominent foreign commercial enterprises in China, such as the Shanghai Electric Power Company and the Shanghai Telephone Company, issued tens of millions of dollars worth of preferred stocks and bonds each time. Even Shanghai municipal bonds were handled by them. At that time, the average return on securities listed in the public exchange was only six to seven percent per annum, which was significantly lower compared to the returns on securities listed on the Chinese commercial securities exchange, which often exceeded one percent per annum. Chinese industrialists only knew to complain about the excessive burden of interest, but they were unaware that the deficiencies in the structure of the capital market had long created unfavorable conditions for Chinese industrialists. The phenomenon of foreign commercial securities predominating in the market, and the phenomenon of foreign dominance in commercial operations, had a direct causal relationship. Conversely, in the Chinese commercial securities exchange, stock listings were rare, and almost all transactions were the buying and selling of government bonds. As a result of this deformed development, the Chinese commercial securities exchange had become a purely fiscal securities market, rather than a long-term capital market for industry and commerce. Industrialists and merchants had no means to issue stocks and corporate bonds, and had to borrow short-term funds for long-term capital use. The drawbacks of this were that the financial industry had one more type of claim that was prone to freezing, while industry and commerce, in addition to bearing high interest rates, faced the risk of being forced to repay debts at any time. In short, if an industrial securities market is not established, the corporate organization will not be able to develop. It will be difficult to start new industries, and it will be difficult for existing industries to survive. Due to the deficiencies in the structure of the long-term capital market, foreign investment in China tended towards the real estate in the concessions. Chinese people followed suit, and the business policies of some foreign banks not only recognized the real estate deeds in the concessions as targets for long-term loans, but even considered them as collateral for short-term financing. Their high liquidity was almost the same as that of the first-class securities and bills in various countries, which was a rare phenomenon in the financial history of various countries. As a result of this deformed development, not only did Shanghai capital flow into real estate instead of productive industries, but even inland capital flowed into Shanghai for real estate speculation. At that time, real estate deeds were not only the most liquid credit instrument, but also the most valuable credit instrument. The value of real estate in the Shanghai Public Concession and the French Concession, based on land price alone, had reached 1.4 billion yuan according to the valuation of the municipal authorities. Even today, although times have changed, its serious impact on the national economy is still worthy of deep consideration. (To be continued)

Spring and Autumn

Tidbits

— (Zhu Weixuan)

A brand-new piece of clothing, suddenly stained with a stain, is certainly unsightly and makes people hate it, but the stain on the clothing can be removed, and if it cannot, at most only one piece of clothing is sacrificed. Only a stain on one's character is a lifelong defect, a permanent blemish. However, people in today's society often ignore the stain on their character, and instead fuss over the blemish on their clothing.

In the trams of Beiping, it is often seen that young men in suits and leather shoes give their seats to (modern) women. It is said that this is because women are physically weak and cannot bear the burden of standing, so it is an action that polite young people should take; but I wonder what these polite young people would think if they saw women and their husbands carrying sedan chairs up the mountain while hiking? Perhaps they would be sitting comfortably in the sedan chair, and still be saying that they are not strong enough and do not walk fast enough!

After a person dies, if the portrait hanging in the True Likeness Pavilion is somewhat similar to the person's appearance before death, it will immediately be discovered and cannot be concealed at all; however, the elegiac couplets praising their merits hanging next to the True Likeness Pavilion, and the grand eulogy and mournful account of their deeds in their obituary, although completely inconsistent with the person's reality before death, no one will criticize them. This is truly a great question!

Huishan Clay Figures

— Rong Yu

A friend from Wuxi sent me two clay figures produced in Huishan, one is a curly-haired fashionable girl, and the other is a naked woman with protruding breasts. I am ashamed that I am not an artist and have no way to appreciate them, so I have to give them to my two children at home to play with.

Speaking of the clay figures of Xishan, they also have a long history in small crafts; and they are also famous far and wide. I remember when I was a child, when I was "worshipping Buddha" with my neighborhood friends, I was playing with this kind of thing. There were Big Afu figures with fat heads and big ears, with a bun on their heads, and a big belly; there were also Wenchang figures with white faces and long beards, wearing red robes; and there were also Zhao Xuantan figures holding whips and riding tigers with golden faces. These were all products of Huishan, and we children treasured them like precious gems. Now that times have advanced, the kinds mentioned above are only for children in the countryside to play with, and the current sculptures are mostly of models, children, and fashionable girls; there are also Liu Guan Zhang's oath of brotherhood, and the Three Stars of Fortune, Prosperity, and Longevity. Belonging to the dramatic aspects, such as the civet cat for the prince, the wax temple, and Baishuitan. There are also Peking Opera faces, with all kinds of roles, such as sheng, dan, jing, and chou; but there are only heads and faces without bodies, only for a few opera fans to enjoy.

The shaping of a clay figure also involves several steps: first, mixing the clay, second, making the embryo, third, coloring, and fourth, applying oil. There are hundreds of families at the foot of Huishan who rely on it for a living! However, I hope that they will further improve, imitating the method of Western plaster statues, to sculpt all kinds of figures. The colors should not be gaudy, but should strive for elegance and generosity; the postures should also be lively and vivid, and should not fall into vulgarity and dullness, so that they will not worry about not occupying a place in the art world!

Transformation

— Da Mu

Old Ke has changed. He gets angry at the drop of a hat and says, "I don't want friends anymore. Friends have deceived me enough. My spirit is also suffering enough. Let me be alone." He moved his room from Tangjia Lane to the Sun Temple to live in. He doesn't write letters to people, and he doesn't reply to letters that people send him. He works as a (errand boy) in a large hotel. Many women with flamboyant outfits pass before his eyes all day and night. He always mutters in his throat: "Women, unreliable women, you either chase after foreign money or fall in love with pretty boys. Old Ke, alas, Old Ke has suffered enough from you..."

Old Ke is not yet twenty-eight years old, but he looks like he is close to forty. He has been through the hardships of the world since he was a child without a home or family. He has a natural and generous temperament with many friends, and his face full of short beards has the style of "Hu Dahai," but he can write unrestrained erotic poems. He often subtly expresses to his friends that he lacks the comfort of the opposite sex. Later, through the introduction of friends, he also met several girlfriends! Female clerks, female poets, female students, singing stars...

However, he was all abandoned halfway. Some girlfriends ran away with his friends. So, he cursed all his friends: "You have deceived me spiritually. You have stolen my soul and loyalty!" In the past, he had given up alcohol, quit smoking, and stopped writing poetry for his girlfriends... He had been a submissive follower for a period of time. Now, his pink dream is shattered, and he always hides alone in his room drinking, drinking... cursing...

"Old Ke has changed, he's gone crazy," friends all tell each other indifferently.

Little Western Paradise

— Written by Zhang Henshui

Chapter 19: The High Official Cherishes His Reputation and Knows How to Knock on Doors, A New Love Leaves Her Flesh and Blood, Visiting the Sick is Impossible

When Jie Fu saw his situation, he knew that he was more anxious than Lan Zhuanshi, so he smiled and said: "Then, I will go." As he spoke, he walked towards Jia Duocai's side. This was really embarrassing enough. Seeing that Secretary Qiu was loyal to his master, always looking at people from above, not allowing him to retreat, he slowly walked to the door of Jia Duocai's room, but saw that the light in his room was as small as a bean. Through the dim paper window, it was easiest to see this little bit of light. Jia Duocai made no sound, but he heard the little girl Yueying crying again. This was really difficult to handle. If he called out to Mr. Jia at this time, he would not be happy. And Yueying was still crying. If he spoke through the window, he was even more afraid that people would say that he was exploring secrets. After hesitating for a while, he looked at the upstairs again, guessing that Ze Cheng was in a high and bright place, unable to see this dark and low place. So, he walked to the corner of the wall and, talking to himself, deliberately imitating Jia Duocai's accent, said in a low voice: "Since you have come and said this, I will give you face and not hold it against you." Then he said in his own voice: "Thank you, thank you, I will treat you to dinner in the future." After muttering for a while, he said loudly: "Okay! We have an agreement." Only then did he leave the corner of the wall, deliberately passing under the stairs, and going to the side of Zhou Yourong's room. His room was in a small courtyard, which Ze Cheng could not see even if he was standing upstairs in the east building. This was much more generous. He stood in the middle of the small courtyard, looked at the stars in the sky for a while, estimating that it had been eight or ten minutes, before turning around and walking out of the courtyard. Ze Cheng seemed to take this matter very seriously, and he was still standing by the railing upstairs. Jie Fu suddenly had a thought in his heart, and he had a brilliant plan. He quickened his pace and ran up the stairs. (323)

Records of Imperial Incense Drifting

— Originally written by Princess Deling of the Qing Dynasty, translated by Qin Shouou

In addition to Danfeng Chaoyang, other more valuable chrysanthemums include Bailongxu, Zijinling, Xueqiu, and Yuguotianqing, several dozen kinds, one (page) is not enough to list them; (even if) they are listed, there is no interest, so here is determined to omit them all.

The Empress Dowager's love for flowers is very much in the style of a scholar. She certainly does not limit her love to mere appreciation: she wants to fully utilize them for every kind of flower. For example, she takes various fresh flowers to be used as specimens for the female workers who do embroidery, and she makes cosmetics from the juice of roses and phoenix flowers, all of which are very meaningful. So, how does the Empress Dowager use chrysanthemums? She uses (them) as food in the following way:

First, she picks one or two (blooms) of the white chrysanthemum called Xueqiu, probably because the petals of Xueqiu are short and dense, and very clean, so they are especially suitable for cooking; she always picks and eats them. After picking them, she plucks all the petals together, picks out those that are scorched yellow or have dirt on them and throws them away, then immerses the remaining ones in warm water for one or two minutes, then takes them out, and then puts them in warm water that has been dissolved with alum, and finally scoops them up, puts them in a bamboo basket to drain, and that is considered to be properly prepared. The second step is, of course, the beginning of cooking. The Empress Dowager is always very excited before trying this special food, like a villager who is about to attend a feast. (423)

World News

The Art of Tattooing in England

— Hai Ke

In London, the capital of England, there is a European-renowned tattoo expert named Gilbert, whose office is on North Lambeth Street. His door is like a market, and people come to him every day to have flowers or characters tattooed on their bodies to leave a permanent souvenir. There are young people, (middle-aged) people, good people, rich people, beautiful girls, even sailors, businessmen, and thieves, all going to ask him to tattoo flowers or characters on their bodies to leave a permanent memento. Once a flower or character is tattooed on, it will never disappear. If you want to change the design, you have to find a way to cover the old design with a new design. If you must remove it, it will take a lot of time and effort, and the handling fee will be considerable.

In general, young people in love often run to Gilbert's door and ask him to tattoo a little Cupid or two hearts on their chest or back, and even tattoo the name of his lover next to it, such as Mary, Joan, Anna, and so on. Young and beautiful women also like this tattooing game very much. There was once a beautiful girl of about twenty years old who, because she fell in love with a young man named White, specially asked Gilbert to tattoo the words "I Love White" on her snow-white jade back and left happily. A week later, she suddenly rushed back to find Gilbert, saying that White was angry with her and she now wanted to remove the words tattooed on her back. Gilbert advised her to be patient and wait a few days, perhaps she would regain her previous feelings, so as to avoid this trouble. But the girl's attitude was very firm and she had to remove it. Gilbert had no choice but to spend two weeks of labor, using an electric needle and a specially made potion to carefully rub it off.

Gilbert regards this kind of work of erasing old words or designs as a difficult task, so he sometimes advises people to change the words into a bunch of flowers, a fresh fruit, a scale of vegetables, or a string of ivy leaves. Relying on his skills, he can cover up those words so that they cannot be seen at all. This kind of work, although troublesome, is much easier than completely erasing it.

According to Gilbert's interview with a reporter from a London weekly, "I have been doing this tattooing work for thirty-five years, and the most strange experience is: one day, a middle-aged man rushed to my shop and asked me to tattoo his entire will on his back. I used to think that it was a fable when I read the novel 'Jade Snow Leaves Traces' by the famous novelist Haggard, which recorded a girl tattooing her will on her shoulders and back. I never thought that someone would actually come to my door and ask me to tattoo a will. This time, the work took me two and a half hours, because the number of words was very large. This will contained a large amount of assets, which were to be distributed to several people in the future. The reason why he wanted to tattoo it on his back was because he would not lose it, and secondly, others could not change it after his death.

According to Gilbert, "The Samoan Islands have the custom of tattooing. Every time they have a child, they have to tattoo the child's date of birth and name on their (body), which will never fade until death. If you want to know who he is in the future, you only need to look at his body to know. A very famous international banker wanted to inspect everything in several branches in India. He tattooed his name on the kidneys above his elbows and instructed his subordinates on detailed strategies. If a person from a distant branch suspects his origins, then he only needs to roll up the sleeves of his shirt; he can prove that he is indeed their leader.

Gilbert also said that love and war are the two driving forces behind tattooing. Therefore, men and women in love often tattoo the names of their lovers on their bodies, or pictures to commemorate their lovers; and after the European war, there were countless soldiers who returned injured. In order to cover up those scars, they came to Gilbert to tattoo a flower or a few words. Therefore, Gilbert's business is extremely developed.

Gilbert's patching skills are indeed very clever. There was a woman who had an external disease on her cheek and was treated by a surgeon who cut it open and stitched up the wound. But that line of trace was still faintly visible. The woman had this blemish on her jade-like beautiful cheek and thought it was the greatest regret of her life. One day, she came to visit Gilbert and asked him to find a way to make up for it, not hesitating to pay a generous reward. Gilbert used his magical surgery and actually made up for it perfectly, as if it were seamless, making the woman happy and amazed.

Gilbert is also a beauty expert, and his wife gave him a great advertisement. Twenty years ago, he had performed a surgery on her face, and her face still looks like a peach blossom, as delicate as a sixteen or seventeen-year-old girl. At first, Gilbert had tattooed some pink patterns on his wife's arm, which looked extraordinarily charming. When his middle-aged girlfriend saw it, she asked Gilbert to tattoo such a touch of pink color on her face as well. Gilbert did as he was told, making this girlfriend seem to have regained her youth. She was extremely satisfied and spread the news of his ability to beautify.

Gilbert also said, "My most interesting customer was an old man with white hair in his seventies. He rushed to see me and asked me to tattoo a touch of pink color on his face. According to him, he wanted to look like an old sailor, looking healthy and ruddy. I certainly did it, and the old man was satisfied and left. My most arduous task was when an Australian official was about to go abroad to take office and asked me to tattoo a very complicated picture on his back. This time, I started from 7:30 in the morning and did not finish until midnight. One of my most difficult tasks was when a gambler had just won a big sum of money in the casino and was very happy. He came and asked me to tattoo a full deck of cards on his back to commemorate it. One of my most proud works was when an old gentleman came and asked me to tattoo a likeness of His Majesty King George on his smooth bald head to express his enthusiasm for loyalty to the King and love for the country."

Java Decides to Send Xu Chengji to Participate in the National Games

Returning to the Country by Ship on the 25th of This Month; Zeng Duancai and Xu Chengwei Together

Java Correspondence: Mr. Xu Chengji, who was selected from Taiwan, returned to Java from Shanghai recently. The Chinese Tennis Federation of Batavia held a reception at the Zhongyuan Restaurant that evening to welcome Mr. Xu. During the gathering, the matter of sending representatives to this year's National Games was discussed. Although the leaders acknowledged the current economic downturn and the difficulty of raising funds, they believed that efforts must be made to promote sports in Java. As a result of the discussions, it was decided to send three people: Xu Chengji, Zeng Duancai, and Xu Chengwei. Zeng Duancai is the singles champion of Surabaya this year. He recently came to Batavia with Japanese student athletes for a performance. Although his strength is slightly inferior, he is still an outstanding talent in our overseas Chinese tennis community. Xu Chengwei is Mr. Xu Chengji's younger brother, young and strong, with a promising future. This year, he won the doubles championship in the Surabaya-Semarang inter-city competition. This time, he will also be attending the National Games as a doubles partner. Mr. Xu Chengji returned to Solo early this morning and is scheduled to come to Batavia on the 21st of this month for an exhibition match to raise funds. The date of his return to China is set for September 25th. His younger brother and Zeng Duancai will also come to Batavia on the 21st if possible. Yesterday afternoon, Mr. Xu practiced at the Chinese sports field. His hitting technique has improved significantly, and he often uses extreme speed. For example, when intercepting a shot, if the position is not good, most people will take a step back to hit a half-volley, but Mr. Xu instead takes a step forward to smash the ball. This is a matter of "timing." The saying "a difference of a hair's breadth leads to a difference of a thousand miles" has become important in modern tennis technique. His serving technique has also changed. His "style one" involves slightly bending at the waist when serving, aiming to make the ball swift and spinning. After practice, Mr. Xu briefly discussed the tennis atmosphere in the United States. He said that tennis has become widespread among American children. Those who are thirteen or fourteen years old hit the ball hard and powerfully. During practice, they generally use "Edison" brand tennis balls, which have weak elasticity but are sturdy. Unless one hits the ball with full force, it is difficult to get it over the net. Under these circumstances, when American children hit a ball, they almost "exhaust all their strength." Therefore, their wrist strength will be astonishing when they grow up. This kind of training method may be difficult to emulate due to the physiques of overseas Chinese children, but it is worthy of attention in our overseas Chinese tennis community. The reporter hopes that the authorities of the Chinese Tennis Federation of Batavia will, if possible, restrict the types of balls used by its members. Any tennis balls that are light and easily moved should be banned. This may make a significant contribution to the development of tennis among overseas Chinese. Recently, when Mr. Xu arrived at Tanjung Priok port, he was photographed on the ship. To the left of Mr. Xu was an American woman. This woman is the advertising director of the Charteris News Agency, named Weiss. After departing from the United States, she and Mr. Xu were on the same ship. Their itineraries were almost identical, from Shanghai to Hong Kong, and from Hong Kong to Java. They often gathered together. Over the long voyage, it seems that Mr. Xu has found a foreign companion, a truly rare and destined relationship. The reporter asked Mr. Xu about this, saying, "The falling flowers have intention, what about your feelings?" Mr. Xu shook his head repeatedly and said, "This is just a friendship from an encounter." Readers may still remember that when Mr. Xu returned to Shanghai years ago to attend a sports event, he once had a crush on Miss , but this matter has now become history. This time, Mr. Xu's return to China from the United States has brought another romance, which is enough to add to the gossip. It is said that the woman went to Bogor yesterday, and will "take a plane to Surabaya, and then travel from Surabaya to Malang." What will become of her after this, is unknown.

Sichuan Athletes Participating in the National Games: Itinerary and Record; Football Team Achieves Complete Victory in Chongqing

(Chongqing Airmail) The Sichuan Athletes Team held a flag-presenting and oath-taking ceremony at the Provincial Government at 4:00 PM on September 6th. On the 17th, they set off eastward and arrived in Chongqing yesterday (the 19th). The situation of the team on the journey and the results of the football team's matches against various teams in Chongqing are reported below.

Diary from Chengdu to Chongqing: On the morning of September 17th, the Sichuan Athletes Team for the Sixth National Games, a group of more than 40 people, led by General Leader Liu Shenzhan, gathered in front of the Minben Sports Teacher's School and departed by car. The athletes team was originally scheduled to depart on September 18th, but due to the convenience of the Superintendent's special car, they advanced the departure by one day. There were three cars in total: one for the female athletes and two for the remaining staff and athletes. Although it was crowded, everyone had a smile on their face. Everyone was happy. The three cars drove out of the East Gate one after another, heading onto the Chengdu-Chongqing Avenue. The weather was good, and the trees and grass in the fields all looked happy and vibrant, just like the people in our cars. When we reached the top of Longquanyi Mountain, we looked back at Chengdu. This area truly deserves to be called a fertile basin for thousands of miles, lying at the bottom of our eyes. We were solemnly touched. It was getting dark, and the car sped through the twilight. The evening breeze blew on our faces, bringing the fragrance of osmanthus flowers from time to time. Around 7:00 PM, we arrived at Qiuxi River and went to bed. The whole team stayed in two hotels. Before going to bed, the staff and the team leaders held a meeting to review the shortcomings discovered on the first day of the trip and to discuss ways to correct them in the future. The fatigue of the day's journey was relieved during the night. Early in the morning of the first day, at only 5:00 AM, everyone climbed back into the car. Today, the car was quiet, no one was laughing, and no one was talking much. Everyone's mood was weighed down by the three words "September 18th." We remembered two lines from the athletes' cheering words: "A strong enemy is pressing on our border, we will resist; we will recover the lost territory in the Northeast." Yes, we undoubtedly want to be warriors for the revival of the nation. As the car approached Neijiang, it started to rain. We silently let the rain fall on us, without moving or making a sound. The first two cars arrived in Neijiang first. When the third car arrived, they stood up solemnly and listened to the athletes' cheering words again, and then calmly jumped out of the car. Breakfast was at the Wan'an Hotel in Neijiang. In my opinion, regardless of whether it rained or not, we should leave immediately after eating, but the driver said we had to wait for the rain to stop, so we had no choice but to silently hope for clear skies. At 12:00 PM, the rain finally stopped, and the car started again. We arrived at Beimuzhen, crossed the river to Rongchang for lunch, and spent the night in Yongchuan. Early in the morning of the 19th, we left Yongchuan again, expecting to arrive in Chongqing at 11:00 AM. The hardship of the past two days was overcome by the thought of reaching Chongqing, and everyone was happy again.

The car with the female athletes was in the lead, and they were very happy because they had left us behind. They showed a competitive spirit everywhere. But in terms of liveliness, our car was the most lively. At around 11:00 AM, the car arrived in Chongqing. We tidied up our clothes outside the city and then entered the city. We contacted the YMCA and used the auditorium as our dormitory. In the afternoon, our football team played against the Chongqing United Team, and the athletes' team won 3-0. If there is an opportunity, the men's and women's basketball teams will also prepare to play here once. The track and field team can also have a competition.

We also decided to leave Chongqing on the Minsheng Company's "Minggui" ship on the 24th and sail directly to Shanghai. Regarding our football team, they left the province on September 4th, arrived in Chongqing on the 5th, and stayed at the Yuzhong Hotel. The next day, they moved to the Public Sports Field. Everything went smoothly. The following is a report from football team captain Zeng Zhengqi to the general leader: (September 6th) During practice at 4:00 PM, they had a temporary match with a mixed team. Because the team members had been overworked in the car for many days and had not recovered their energy, they won 1-0.

(September 9th) They played against the Huashen Team at the Public Sports Field. There were many spectators and the order was good. The field was too small, so the players could not fully display their skills. The opponents' actions were sometimes excessive. For the sake of their own safety, the team members did not use full force. In the first half, they took the lead with a score of 2-0. In the afternoon, each team scored a goal, and the team won 4-2.

(September 14th) They played against the Xiude Club football team. This team is the essence of the Minsheng Company's Navigation Management Office's Kang Travel Team, but their coordination was poor. In addition, our team's cooperation was gradually improving, so the match was not very exciting. It was a one-sided game. In both halves, our team scored six goals, while the Xiude team did not score any. As a result, our team won 11-0. This match was held at the Shanli Middle School field.

(September 17th) They played against the Huatie Team. This team is an incarnation of the Huashen Team. Although our team won 4-0 in this match, ten team members were injured. (September 19th) They played against the Electric Power and Municipal United Team. This team is the essence of Chongqing City, and the talents of Chongqing also have ambitions to defeat our team. Because our team had too many injuries, they requested a postponement, but the other team refused on the grounds that it was difficult to gather their team members, and insisted on playing today. Our team had no choice but to reluctantly agree to start the match at 3:00 PM. The injured team members were injured even more, and they had to be replaced from time to time. Fortunately, there were still many substitutes, otherwise it would have been unimaginable. Neither team scored in the first half. After changing sides, our team changed its strategy and concentrated its attack. Sure enough, within ten minutes, they scored a goal. About five minutes later, they scored again from the left wing. At this time, the enemy was flustered, and our team took the opportunity to attack again and scored another goal. As a result, our team won 3-0. Although the team members were beaten black and blue in this match, they have successively defeated the teams in Chongqing. This is something that the team members are very proud of.

Completion Ceremony of Daxia Gymnasium

Daxia University started construction of the gymnasium in early June of this year. After more than three months, all the construction work has been completed, and it is quite magnificent and grand. In addition to the sports field, the gymnasium also has management rooms, equipment rooms, dressing rooms, shower rooms, and other facilities. All the equipment is in accordance with the latest scientific methods. There are no pillars in the entire gymnasium, and the stands are foldable and can be stored when not in use, which is rare in the country. Yesterday morning, the school held a completion ceremony for the gymnasium. More than a thousand faculty, staff, and students attended. Following the usual procedures, President Wang Boqun delivered a speech, stating that since the school has been implementing national revival education, the need for physical education has become increasingly urgent. Now that the gymnasium has been completed, he hopes that all students will make active and vigorous progress in physical training, and not slacken their efforts, in preparation for shouldering heavy responsibilities in the future. Next, Wu Zelin, representing the villagers of Daxia New Village, presented a construction fee of 10,000 yuan. Fang Wanbang, director of the school's physical education program, and Luo Chuanhua, representing the China Foreign Famine Relief Committee, gave speeches in succession.

Committee for the Implementation of Children's Year Passes Relief Measures for Children in Disaster Areas

(Nanjing, 13th) The National Committee for the Implementation of Children's Year held its third standing committee meeting at the Ministry of Education on the 23rd at 10:00 AM. Children Under Six Years of Age Prohibited from Watching Ordinary Films Joint Announcement by the Bureau of Education, Youth, and Public Safety

The Municipal Bureau of Education and the Bureau of Public Safety, in order to prohibit children under six years of age from watching general films, yesterday issued a joint announcement stating: "We have received Instruction No. 15350 from the Municipal Government, which states: 'With the approval of Document No. 12310 issued by the Ministry of Interior Police Department on August 10th of the 24th year, and Public Letter No. 559 issued by the Propaganda Committee of the Central Executive Committee of the Chinese Kuomintang on August 3rd of the 24th year, and with the approval of a letter sent by the China Educational Film Association, requesting the Central Government to issue a general order to the entire country at the Association's 4th annual meeting, stating that children under six years of age are not allowed to enter ordinary cinemas at any time, except when cinemas are showing children's educational films, which they are specifically allowed to watch. This matter has been referred to the 36th meeting of the Film Industry Guidance Committee of this Association, which resolved to request the Ministry of Interior to consider the matter. After review, there are no objections. Please examine the original proposal attached hereto for reference and provide your opinions on how to handle it. As approved, it is deemed necessary to prohibit children under six years of age from entering ordinary cinemas at any time for the sake of the health of children nationwide. In addition to replying by letter and distributing it, we are copying the original proposal and requesting that you examine it for reference, instruct all cinemas to comply with it, and make a public announcement to make it known to all.' As approved, we are hereby copying and issuing the original proposal and ordering you to comply with it. This order is given, etc., with the attached original proposal. This matter concerns the protection of children's health, and all children's families should understand this intention. In the future, unless educational films for children are being shown, do not bring them to watch. In addition to ordering all cinemas to comply with this order, we are issuing this public announcement to make it known to all. This announcement is made."

Recent News on the National Institute for Compilation and Translation's Compilation of Terminology

The Natural Science Group of the National Institute for Compilation and Translation has recently summarized the progress of its terminology work as follows: (1) Medical Terminology: (A) The third draft of the terminology of psychopathology has been returned by various committee members, including Lin Ji (Peking University Medical College), Lu Dexin (Qilu University), Cheng Yuchen, Wei Yulin (Peking Union Medical College), Qi Shounan, Tao Zuyin (Central Hospital), Gu Jingpai (Shanghai Medical College), Song Guobin, and Lu Yudao (Academia Sinica). It will soon be compiled and sent to press. (B) The anatomical terminology has been supplemented and completed and is ready for mimeographing. The entire manuscript is about 500 pages, and over 300 pages have already been printed. It will be sent for review after all pages have been printed. (2) Botanical Terminology: Yesterday, Mr. Wang Cengjia sent three sets of botanical terminology cards from Peiping, totaling over 700 entries. (3) Mineralogical Terminology: The proofreading has been completed, and Wang is currently compiling the index. (4) Petrological Terminology: Since being submitted for review last year, many experts have returned the material. The terminology includes external dynamic geology, astrogeology, topography, structural geology, crustal movement, volcanology, mineral deposit geology, seismology, and stratigraphy, divided into seven volumes. The first, fourth, and fifth volumes have been compiled. The first volume covers external dynamic geology, astrogeology, and topography, totaling about 3,000 terms. The fourth and fifth volumes cover crustal movement and seismology, totaling about 910 terms. The remaining five volumes are still being compiled. (5) Chemical Engineering Terminology: It is currently undergoing final proofreading and arrangement and is expected to be ready for printing by the end of the month. (6) Chemical Terminology: Nearly 30 volumes of the first draft have been reviewed and returned by experts. (7) Terminology of Embryology: After two years of effort and the enthusiasm of experts, it has now been completed and is being copied to be submitted for promulgation. (8) Terminology of Comparative Anatomy: The first draft has been sent to experts for review and has been returned by Wu Zhaofa, Liu Xian, Lu Yudao, Cai Bao, Yong Kechang, Wen Yichuan, and Xue Liangshu. (9) Mathematical Terminology: The third draft of mathematical terminology, totaling 14 volumes, has been compiled. Statistics of elementary mathematics terminology from arithmetic to elementary calculus, totaling over 2,000 characters, have been compiled and sent to the Mathematical Terminology Review Committee of the Chinese Mathematical Society for review.

Little Boy (55) —Original Work by American Woman Alcott, Translated by Zheng Xiaocang (Zonghai)

One day, a Saturday afternoon, when a group of children came to play, Tao Mo said:

"Let's run to the river and get some new fishing rods back,"

"We'll have Tu Pi drag them back, and one of us can ride him over," proposed Tai Pang, who was most afraid of walking.

"That means you're going to ride, I suppose; well, come on, you lazybones," said Tang En, and he dashed off, later intercepted the poles, just about to return, unfortunately Xiao Qiao saw Tao Mo riding Tu Pi, holding a long pole in his hand, and said:

"You look like that bullfighter in the picture, but you don't have a red scarf, and you're not wearing bright clothes,"

"I want to see one; come on?" Tao Mo blurted, while searching for his spear.

"Then come on; at Old Huang's peanut patch in that big meadow, charge over there, Tao Mo, see how she runs," that always misbehaving Tang En proposed.

"No, you can't," Xiao Qiao began to stop him, he already knew that Tang En's proposal was unreliable.

Tang En cut in and asked, "Why can't you? You little scared girl," "My uncle doesn't like this."

"Has he ever said we can't bullfight?"

"No, I haven't heard him say that," Xiao Qiao also admitted to seeing.

"Then don't open your mouth again, go up, Tao Mo, here's a red strip of cloth to pounce on that thing, I'll help you incite her;" Tang En said, leaping over the wall, he was really excited about that new thing, behind him followed a group of children, who were as docile as a flock of sheep, even Xiao Qiao was among them, he sat on the fence to watch the progress of the game, and also felt a lot of interest.

Free Talk

Thoughts on Reading History

-- Tang Tao

The issue of revising the way history is read was raised a long time ago, and it has been discussed in various forms, but now it has been neglected. In the July issue of the Shenbao last year, Mr. Xu Maoyong advocated that schools should adopt social evolution history as a textbook from the beginning. This opinion is very noteworthy. Social evolution history books are still too alien to modern Chinese students. We only see famous phrases such as "Emperor Wu of Han was a man of great talent and bold strategy" and "The era of ×× can be compared to the reign of Cheng and Kang" swirling in the minds of middle school students. However, they are very vague about the causes and consequences of historical evolution. This is really not a good phenomenon.

Regarding history, I believe that it should not only be revised in how it is read, but also in how it is written. Books on social evolution history are certainly important, but the historical deeds of Emperor Wu of Han, Emperor Taizong of Tang, and others should also be known to some extent. However, there is very little in past history books that can be trusted. Take the privately written history books of the Han and Jin dynasties as an example. Due to limited knowledge and a lack of wide and extensive records, the result can only be a rough sketch. By the Tang Dynasty, Emperor Taizong proclaimed himself to be "respectful of literature," and the state set up a bureau to compile history. Although the collection of materials could be more extensive, the history books were written by officials, so they inevitably had to speak the official line from time to time. The trustworthy component is even less. At this time, everyone had to dig into unofficial history.

However, my reason for saying that history should be revised or rewritten is more than just this. Past historians have focused too much on sculpting heroes and neglected the power of the masses and the social environment that shaped these heroes. What they recorded was the history of a dynasty - in fact, the history of a single family, and in this family, they only wrote about a few characters that they considered important.

But in fact, history is not the history of a few people.

So it must be revised. The so-called revision is certainly not a random alteration of "demons and monsters." Rather, it demands more truthfulness and credibility in historical events. However, on the one hand, it is necessary to use new methods to re-evaluate and inject a progressive world view. In this way, the historical facts of the past can be connected to the current situation, and the causes and consequences of why the present has become the present can be understood. This is the greatest significance of history.

In the middle of the Qing Dynasty, scholars were very enthusiastic about revising and supplementing history. For example, Tang Chenglie's "Book of the Ji Han," Xie Qikun's "Book of the Western Wei," Zhou Ji's "Outline of the Jin," Chen Zhan's "Continuation of the Book of Tang," Shao Jinhan's "Annals of the Song," Wei Yuan's "New History of the Yuan," etc., corrected many errors in the old history, and the writing style also had many new attempts. This perseverance is worthy of admiration.

But there are still shortcomings: Although they knew that there were "red-haired people" outside of themselves, they still did not have a new world view.

Since last year, so-called historical essays have begun to appear in the writing community, which is naturally a gratifying thing. However, there are not many people who write such essays, and even fewer who write well. The reason for this, I think: First, the author must have a correct world view; second, he must have rich historical knowledge. The former focuses on imparting, and the latter focuses on understanding. These are necessary for those who want to rewrite history.

But such talents are hard to come by. In modern times, I only know one: H.G. Wells.

However, for China, I not only hope that there will be good historical essays, but also that there will be a Wells, a complete history book with a correct and new world view, whether it is revised, supplemented, or rewritten. - After reading a history book compiled by a recent person, I thought this so urgently in my heart. September 16th.

The Owner of the Lovebird

-- Zhang Yiping

The owner of the lovebird has a beautiful title called "Playboy." He is very satisfied and proud of this title, although people always call him "Young Master" in his presence.

In the third month of late spring, the peach blossoms outside the city are in full bloom. Spring is a season for travel, and people in the city go to the suburbs in groups. The countryside is sometimes envied by the city people. The young master has been a little sick lately. He is too lazy to even smoke opium, and his trusted servant Genfu has been sent by "Old Master" to do some errand. He spends his days confined in his study, playing with the lovebird that is good at serving people. He pouts his thick lips and imitates its call. When he is happy, he waves his hands and pretends to fly, passing the days with such difficulty. One early morning, he accidentally glanced at a peach tree in the corner of the courtyard, with red flowers blooming. He pounded the window frame with his refined fist. If Genfu were in front of him, he would have figured out a way to while away this sleepy spring. The peach blossoms in the suburbs should be crowded with tourists. The young master thought, grabbed the bird cage and held it in the palm of his right hand, and suddenly set off alone to the suburbs.

But when he returned, the young master was like a defeated rooster, lying listlessly on the opium couch, rolling the finest opium paste on the tip of the flame, and finally turning it into a lump of charcoal. The lovebird, however, was jumping and hopping in its cage, singing even more beautifully, as if telling people that it had encountered something very pleasant in the suburbs. But it is not a myna, so no one can guess what it means, and the young master who can speak is shutting his beak, as if he is annoyed, contrary to the lovebird. He smoked enough opium (without taking a single puff), jumped up from the opium couch, and hung the bird cage under the eaves. It was the bird he loved, otherwise he would have smashed it half to death long ago. When the young master is angry, no one dares to fart. He paced back and forth in the center of the room, bored and annoyed, racking his brains. He thought more urgently of Genfu. If Genfu were by his side, hum, this matter would not be so tricky!

Footsteps stopped at the door of the study. The young master mumbled a Buddhist prayer, but he did not turn around immediately, asking loudly who it was. He pricked up his ears, wanting to hear a low, humble, "Young Master, it's me." Sure enough, Genfu's voice was familiar to his ears. His heart blossomed like a flower, but his face was still tense as he asked, "Is the matter done well?"

Genfu slipped in like a chicken thief. After looking at the young master's face, he said quietly, "It's all a matter of life! I've been working on it for so many days, and I haven't gotten a single penny!" At the same time, he showed a cunning smile, "I'm also thinking that the young master's peach blossoms are blooming (that's tomorrow), and Genfu will serve the young master with an empty body!"

Genfu retreated backwards, and sat unintentionally on the other end of the opium couch. A thick fragrance wafted into his nostrils, and Genfu shrugged his shoulders. "Young master, the opium from the Lu family is really pure. He put on a flattering smile again. He was waiting for the young master to say: Genfu, give me a pipe!

But the young master was not as generous as he imagined. He raised his head and drew circles in the air with the index finger of his right hand. After a long while, he asked Genfu:

"The peach blossom stream turns a bend to the west. What is the place with those big trees, Genfu?"

"That's Yang's village."

Genfu looked at the owner's face carefully. He knew that after doing errands for ten days, the "Playboy" was a little horny. He immediately sat up a little straighter. As long as the young master asked further, he could make it up for the ten days of hard work.

"Are you familiar with that place?"

Genfu laughed: "Young master, I know the city and the countryside, dozens of miles around, like the back of my hand. I'm not bragging. You listen: From the peach blossom stream, turn a bend to the west, and you'll see two big trees. There's a row of two-room thatched cottages. That's the tenant of Master Zhu Chongqing. Further past there's a duck farmer named Zhang Laotou. The ducks for Yulijufeng Hall and Deqing Building are all bought from him. Further past..." Genfu spun his fingers, "Uh, that's the Lu Qicai family. He has a very beautiful daughter..."

The young master suddenly jumped up:

"That's it!"

He rushed to the opium couch. "Genfu, make me a few pipes, and we'll talk slowly!"

Genfu was waiting for these words. He leaned back and lay on the lower end of the opium couch, his left leg crossed over the couch arm. As soon as he dipped the opium with a spoon, he shouted how fragrant, how fragrant, the opium from the Lu family is really rare!

The young master understood what he meant, and he displayed a proud smile.

"Don't act smart in front of me, give me a pipe. But you have to handle this matter for me well!"

"Thank you, young master! Genfu pulled out his empty hand and patted his chest, "Genfu doesn't have any other skills, but this little thing is my specialty!"

He skillfully rolled the opium on his fingers, put it on the pipe bowl, and puffed it twice. Then he called out in surprise in the small tea table nearby:

"Oh, it's ginseng soup, I thought it was tea!"

"As long as you handle things properly, young master will be willing to give you anything. Tell me what method to use to get that little girl, the sooner the better!"

"It's very easy. Genfu said, making opium again, while leaning over and whispering in the young master's ear, "I guarantee you'll get her in three days, but, how will you thank me?"

Genfu used the tricks of a rogue, squinting one eye and staring at the young master. The young master jumped up impatiently from the opium couch: "You name your price!"

"Hahaha..." Genfu laughed like a crow, "I've been eating the young master's food for so many years. Is there a need to ask for a reward for this little thing? Let Genfu smoke one more pipe."

The young master ignored him and slowly walked to the window, reaching out to the window to bring in the bird cage under the eaves. As if he were teasing a child, he pursed his thick lips and called out. The lovebird, good at serving its master, flapped its wings, and chanted "Playboy, Playboy..." (End)

Night March

— Xin Zhuojia

During the Northern Expedition, there was a time when, to avoid a direct confrontation with the enemy, we took a large detour and retreated to a steep mountain. It was already very late at night, but we had to continue climbing over the mountain before dawn to reunite with our main force. Our company, with scouts ahead, was exhausted like a dead snake. Three days and three nights of hunger and relentless marching were like the giant hand of a terrifying demon, tightly gripping our throats. Our eyes had lost their gleam, our nostrils were emitting a faint smoke, and our limbs felt as if the tendons had been pulled out and then beaten to a pulp. There was only one shared, clear thought: to sleep, to drink, and to eat. Drinking water was more important than eating, and sleep was even more important than drinking water.

A cook, carrying a pot on his shoulder pole, walked along, dreaming. Vaguely, he and his load tumbled into a foul-smelling ditch.

But we still couldn't rest. And even greater nocturnal hardships were upon us.

We had no idea how high the dark, silent mountain blocking our path actually was. We looked up at the sky, which was black, without stars or moon. We couldn't tell where the boundary between the sky and the mountain peaks lay. Perhaps the peaks were even higher than the sky, perhaps what we were looking at wasn't the sky at all, but merely the cliff face of the mountain. In short—we couldn't see anything.

We groped blindly, as if in a dream, one behind the other, tightly grasping the heels of the brother in front. The mountain path gradually went from sloping to overhanging, to narrow, to winding... Sharp stones stood up like steel thorns.

As our eyes blurred, our minds felt even heavier and more muddled. If it weren't for the sharp stones occasionally tearing our skin and stinging the soles of our feet, we would have simply stood or fallen asleep without realizing it. The aimless wails of nocturnal beasts and the howling of the mountain wind, though constantly vibrating our eardrums, went unnoticed; because, except for hunger, thirst, and sleep, the entire world had long disappeared around us.

We don't know which of the brothers climbing ahead lost his footing and dislodged a large rock or something, which rumbled down into the bottomless mountain stream. The officers then angrily issued orders:

"If anyone can't endure it, if anyone is careless!... If anyone disobeys orders!..."

However, next: Another sound, two sounds... mixed with sharp cries, heavily and flexibly rolled down!

This clearly wasn't the sound of rocks falling!

The troop immediately stopped. And this sudden, strange stimulus caused a huge uproar!

"What's wrong? Who? What happened?..." the officers shouted anxiously! Because they couldn't climb to the front to investigate, they could only shout anxious questions from afar.

"Report: The road ahead is getting narrower!... Less than a foot wide, and we can't see anything!... We can't even find the markings the scouts made!... Two people have fallen down!..."

"No!... We can't stop here!" the officers shouted even more harshly, ordering: "If anyone is careless!... If anyone disobeys orders!..."

"Report—we really can't climb anymore! Our stomachs are empty, our mouths are dry, and our eyes can't see!..."

"Shoot them! Who disobeys orders?..."

Three or four minutes later, we were climbing again, fearfully, mechanically, and deliriously. Everyone's body was completely out of their control. There was only one hope—that dawn would appear immediately, that we would climb over the mountain top, reunite with our main force, and sleep soundly for a whole week, day and night!

When this painful climb had continued for quite a long time, and we touched the special markings left by the scouts—that we were almost at the top of the mountain—our progress suddenly stopped again. This time, however, it wasn't that people had fallen, but that something had blocked our difficult road ahead!

"Report—the front has completely collapsed! We can't see clearly how wide or narrow it is, we can't climb a single step past it!..."

"Then, what about the scouts?" the officers asked with suspicion.

"We don't know!..."

A very ominous sign suddenly stimulated the officers' muddled minds! "Yes," they discussed among themselves, "we should immediately send two messengers to report to the main force behind!... We can only stop here for now. Let the engineering company arrive and then find a way to open a temporary path!... Perhaps, it will be dawn soon!..."

We considered this an unexpected, best opportunity for us to rest, although we knew the danger was very great!... Our backs leaning against the rock wall, our feet went weak, and our eyelids came together as if attracted by a magnet. Our whole body floated up. The god of sleep used his black, large wings, to draw out our weary souls!

We had no idea when dawn appeared. When the officers ordered the squad leaders to pull our ears and pound our heads to wake us up, we had already seen our rear troops winding up. And immediately, a row of dense, fierce enemy fire resounded from the opposite mountain peak!...

We instinctively held our guns, opened the safety, and listened to the orders recited by the squad leaders. Because I had no cover, I hurriedly and clumsily lay down on the spot and began to counterattack fiercely!...

The Suicide (1)

— Qian Dong

The night is late.

Dr. Lan closed the door with a crisp sound, bang! Even the ambulance that had driven out of the hospital could be heard, with the rustling of its tires turning on the sound of the emergency room. The night is very quiet.

Dr. Lan yawned, frowned, and reached out to the five hundred candlepower light in the middle of the emergency room, preparing to see what time it was now? Suddenly, he turned his head, as if he heard something ringing, his eyes startled, and he immediately returned to normal, his face waiting for the elevator outside the door.

The elevator came down. A pastor wearing a black hat, black tuxedo, and a full beard hurriedly walked out. His left hand tightly held a black leather bag, and his right hand was holding a handkerchief to wipe his blood-red nose. This seemed to be his habitual action. He wiped it, and the big nose was temporarily calm, and after a while, beads of sweat appeared again, so he wiped it again.

He moved his thick eyebrows, put the leather bag on the bench, and a joyful, powerful throat sound rang under the handkerchief wiping his nose.

"Dr. Lan, they said the ambulance went out, and it's another suicide. Is it?"

"Yes." Dr. Lan yawned lazily again, pacing around the operating bed.

"Good, then, you," the pastor shouted excitedly, wiping the handkerchief again, "you have to be careful! A suicide when he repents is more profound than ordinary people, because a suicide is more able to appreciate his own sins than ordinary people!"

The pastor smiled, a smile that can only be seen on the face of an innocent child. And the voice was very loud, Huo Huo Huo Huo! Dr. Lan was startled by him, stopped for a moment, glanced at him, and then continued to pace slowly step by step.

The pastor felt that his words were too clever and could already elicit other people's surprise, and immediately called out more proudly:

"I remember again, I also remember, that countryman who was discharged from the hospital this morning, Dr. Lan, do you remember?"

"Which one?" Dr. Lan said indifferently, still walking around in his circle.

"It's the countryman who came in yesterday. He hanged himself from a tree next to Jiangwan Road with a rope. This idiot, if there were no street lights there, he could really achieve his goal. Isn't it? When he woke up here, you asked him: "Why do you want to commit suicide? It's so much trouble for people!" I remember he said bitterly that he was a farmer, and because of the flood in the countryside, he ran to Shanghai, and he also grew vegetables and worked as a porter in Shanghai. Now he doesn't even do these things, only suicide. It's that man, it's that one!"
