Shen Bao Local Supplement

Talk

Two Startling Major Cases

— Meng Ruo

Recently, two startling major cases have occurred in the country, one is the major robbery case in Shouguang County, and the other is the major kidnapping case in Tianjin.

Jinan News: On the 28th of last month, the Shouguang County Nanhe Elementary School was suddenly invaded by more than twenty bandits, who surrounded the school. The principal and teachers had gone to the Fuxing Oil Mill to see the new machinery, so they were not at the school. The bandits tied up more than fifty people, excluding six female students, with thin hemp ropes. Before leaving, they fired more than two hundred gunshots and crossed the surrounding wall. More than twenty children under the age of ten were too weak to support themselves and were sent back. When they reached Zhuobei Village, three students escaped and returned. When they reached Yingzi Village, another student escaped and returned. It is said that the bandits' movements were unusually slow because they were carrying students. After the case occurred, the county magistrate was very anxious and immediately sent teams to intercept and pursue them, but there was no suitable rescue method. It is heard that the principal, together with the parents of the students, will go to the province to petition soon, in order to rescue them as soon as possible.

Tianjin News: The authorities of the British, French, and Japanese concessions in Tianjin successively exhumed seven male corpses who had been kidnapped, strangled, and buried alive by bandits in Lixingli, Tongshenli, Zhuyuanli, Yongfengli, Taichangli, and other places on the 17th. The deaths were very tragic. The criminals in this case were arrested by the British and French Municipal Council, with the cooperation of seven detectives, including one female bandit. In the investigation, the bandits lured the hostages to the destination for killing through the women, and then sent letters to the family members of the victims to demand ransom. According to police investigation, this group of bandits has been active in Pingjin for two years.

These two cases are indeed very shocking. More than twenty bandits in Shouguang County dared to openly break into the Nanhe Elementary School in broad daylight and take away more than fifty students. The seriousness of this situation is extremely worthy of concern. Kidnapping incidents are often heard in our country, but there has never been a case of looting an elementary school and looting more than fifty people at a time. Only extremely heinous bandits have the courage to take risks in this kind of lawless behavior. Judging from the purpose of kidnapping, it is probably to sell them to various places. From the point of view of the situation, it seems very easy to solve this matter. On the one hand, the bandits' movements have been slow because they are carrying students, and on the other hand, several students have escaped and returned, so there should be a clue to be found. However, the county government sent teams to intercept and pursue them separately, but in the end there was no suitable rescue method, allowing the bandits to escape calmly, which is really a pity. If the authorities do not quickly find a way to rescue them in the future, not only will dozens of elementary school students not be rescued, but such robbery cases may be repeated. The issue of responsibility is even more important.

As for the major kidnapping case in Tianjin, the seriousness of the situation is also not to be ignored. Originally, the purpose of kidnapping is to demand ransom, and bandits will never tear up the ticket unless it is absolutely necessary. However, these bandits lured the hostages to the destination for killing through the women, and then sent letters to the family members of the victims to demand ransom. Their behavior is extremely cruel. There is one thing that is particularly worthy of attention in the occurrence of this case, that is, the seven corpses were all exhumed in the concession. Concessions in our country often become places for a group of bandits to do evil. This is related to our country's public security and is truly not a small matter. Moreover, this group of bandits has been active in the Pingjin area for two years, and the scale and organization are undoubtedly strict. Now that the authorities have arrested seven bandits, they should conduct a rigorous investigation in order to eliminate the bandits and prevent future troubles. This is what we most hope for.

Little Song Under the Wheel

— Green Leaf

My life and my nature are obviously in different boundaries; that gray life is constantly honing me, and youth is buried under the wheels, and time is constantly eroding my life. In my heart, in the rosy childhood, there is a kind of gold mine hidden, which contains the life aspirations of forest-colored apples, that is, the life of a bold and unrestrained vagrant, which can only be hidden forever.

(I am thinking of my wish, that there is a beautiful gold mine hidden, in the life of a free and unrestrained vagrant, I also want to be a drummer on the sea, a wandering pirate on a deserted island.)

When can I forget the crushing under the belt wheels? I also have a flying, unrestrained, and great spirit, which makes me have a kind of nostalgia for exile overseas, and that life will be completely in the rose-colored inside, a rough and simple life! I can pick up golden shells on the beach with a group of rough and tall vagrants, or drink heartily and sing forgetfully, singing this pink love song of the vagrants; thinking of the curry, a unique product of India, a spicy taste that can sting the tip of the tongue with new stimulation, and the interesting scenery of Siberia, where the north wind and cold always occupy the world; and then remember the durian and coconut with the southern flavors of the equator, that kind of sweet taste, which is enviable. Here and there, there is no restraint of the cruel belt wheels, I am a free little bird, and I will always miss this rough life.

Under the wheels, the souls of many young guys have been ground. Thinking about it, the belts and wheels will always be cursed and scolded by me. Cemetery, a burst of shivering and fear, and the bones of the white bones seem to flash in front of my eyes; it is the memory buried by the times, and at this time, I can no longer remember the demise of many young men in the long years in this gray life.

I am looking forward to listening to the pine waves of the deserted island and a piece of rare and beautiful autumn scenery in the life of a forest-colored vagrant; at night, watching the beautiful stars on the sea, weaving densely in the sky, like a group of children in paradise, at that time I can remember the simplicity and joy of the rose-colored childhood, and chat with a group of vagrants about the old feelings, and bursts of rough and straightforward laughter are embellished in our encounters. We can tease each other about our infatuation and the interesting stories of women. There is only innocence and loyalty here.

Speaking of stars, I am a little melancholy. In our narrow house, there is a window in the back, or a side door. Only on the roof, a small skylight is framed. On a night with a few sparse stars, you can see three or four stars inlaid on the skylight. One or two lines of green light shoot down, weaving in the rapid rotation of the wheels. The shadow of the wheels is gradually expanding, slowly covering the entire house.

But now, one or two sparse stars of frost flowers are also decorated in the black hair, and in the process under the belt wheels, my youth has long been buried, and I have never received some warmth and comfort in autumn and spring.

The heart is already in the ashes, without warmth and light, gradually peeling off like a rock over time, and the torrent of time has swept away the life of the vagrant's dream that is hidden in my heart and has a rich and golden quality.

The world under the wheels!…

Ode to a Cold

— Hu Si

Whenever the seasons change, I often catch a cold. First, my body is weak, and I was born insufficient, and the postnatal maintenance is not complete. Recently, due to the urgency of life, I have not been able to take care of the trivial matters around me, and I have not been able to take care of my own safety, so small illnesses such as "cold and headache" are naturally easy to invade, and a few days of dizziness and eye swelling are unavoidable.

It is natural to say that a cold is a minor illness because it can heal itself without taking medicine. People who have no money do not care about getting sick. Although it is said that wealthy hygienists advocate that a cold is not a minor disease, because once the disease invades the lungs, it is not a joke. However, for a poor writer, it is better to suffer from a "home disease" like a cold than to suffer from a "hospital disease" (that is, it is impossible not to go to the hospital). Because lung involvement is ultimately rare, and in times of poverty, it is a serious matter to spend money.

But it is not necessarily true to say that a cold does not hinder anything. Once you catch a cold, it goes without saying that you will have dizziness and eye swelling, and you will cry and have a runny nose all day long. It is dizzy to read books and there is no interest at all; it is also impossible to write articles and there is no inspiration to speak of. Even if you reluctantly pick up the pen, you

Page 16

You must keep a wet towel on one side, wipe your tears and snot on one side, and wave the pen on the paper on the other. You must be careful if you sneeze occasionally; otherwise, if water droplets are sprayed on the paper, the work of writing will be greatly hindered.

For those who rely on selling articles for a living, spirit is an indispensable living resource. Once the spirit is lacking, you will be listless all day long and sink into a hazy state, so you cannot write articles and your life will lose its guarantee. The disaster of a cold for poor writers is that it is enough to make the spirit exhausted and unmotivated, and the brain declines, which indirectly hits the works and life. Therefore, the fear of colds by writers is actually no different from that of wealthy hygienists. However, "the rain harms the right to be light." If they suffer from other diseases that require spending money, it is better to have a cold. That is the wishful thinking of the poor people, and the calculations will not be wrong. --Of course, it is best to be an iron bull, completely free from dizziness and stomach pain. But how many people are there in the world, especially writers who are malnourished and have little rest, who can completely avoid illness?

What is even more annoying is that once you catch a cold, it will take several days to recover. There is nothing you can do about this. You have to let the tears and snot flow and drip constantly until you feel refreshed. You also have to let the dizziness and eye swelling be full before there is a solution. But for a person who has no food to eat without writing an article a day, what do you think this will do to him?

Because of a cold, it is easier to feel sentimental. People's tempers are as changeable as wind and clouds. Ordinary gentle temperament, lively mind, after a few days of dizziness and eye swelling, and a crying face, will be frustrated and decadent, and show a self-abandoning mood and behavior. Naturally, people are no longer children, so of course they lack the care of a loving mother; what's more, if they are single, or their lover is not around, the sorrow at that time will be even greater, and or kinds of ridiculous and pitiful actions will be made; or kinds of boring feelings or thoughts will be triggered. Is this unavoidable for literati with strong nervousness? I think some great writers may write famous sentimental articles in their cold times? This is not entirely forgetting and fantasy, I dare say.

Malacca

— From Long

Malacca, known as the "Ancient Coconut City," is filled with historical sites and scenic spots. Its beautiful scenery rivals even Jinling, famous for its six dynasties of splendor. One can never tire of exploring it.

It is said that the scenery of Taiping Lake is the best in the South Seas, but unfortunately, I have not visited it and have not been able to appreciate it. However, I have visited Seremban many times. Although it lacks the tranquil and poetic waterscape, its lush mountains and the verdant Royal Hill are truly worthy of being called "blessed with the spirits of the mountains!" People who have been to Taiping Lake say that "Seremban is one notch above Taiping." This is because Seremban's beauty lies in its verdant mountains. If you stroll along the winding paths of Royal Hill, you can experience the unique and delightful feeling of "when you think you have reached the end of the mountains and rivers and there is no road, suddenly you see a village with willows and bright flowers." Although Malacca is surrounded by mountains and water, it does not have the lush hills of Seremban. Otherwise, the mountains and waters of this "Ancient Coconut City" would be no less than those of Switzerland in Southern Europe!

Malacca has always been famous in history and legend. However, with the development of shipping and because its harbor is too shallow, it cannot accommodate large mail ships. As a result, it has lost its position as a major international port. Nevertheless, it occupies an important page in world history. Just from the historical significance of its role in connecting modern Eastern and Western cultures, it cannot be ignored or erased. In 1377, the newly rising Menjapahit Kingdom of Java conquered the Lion Island and Palembang Kingdom. As a result, Malacca became the only refuge for the Malays and established the Malacca Kingdom here. During its cultural peak, it was famous far and wide. Our country also sent envoys here. According to the Ming History, Zheng He's southern voyages during the Yongle period of the Ming Dynasty (1405) included the official recognition of this place. Malacca was also the first colony acquired by Europeans in the East. In 1511, the Portuguese general Afonso de Albuquerque led a fleet to occupy it. The buildings from that time still exist today, allowing tourists to reminisce and pay homage. Therefore, most people who visit the South Seas always take a trip to Malacca.

"St. Paul's Hill" is one of Malacca's historical sites, but the name of this hill has changed frequently. It originally varied according to the name of the church on the hill. During the Portuguese era, a church dedicated to the Holy Mother was built on top of the hill. Therefore, the hill was called St. Mary's Hill. During the Dutch era, St. Paul's Church was rebuilt, so the hill was renamed St. Paul's Hill. This ancient church was destroyed by gunfire when the Dutch captured Malacca. Now, only the four walls and the tombstone remain. When we enter this ancient church, we see weeds and moss growing in the crevices, and we naturally feel a sense of desolation and horror after the war. To preserve this historical site, the Historical Society erected an ancient monument inside the church. In the center of the altar, there is an underground vault covered with iron bars, which is said to be the burial place of Father Francis. According to elderly people familiar with Malacca, the remains of this priest were moved to "Goa" in India in 1553.

In front of the ancient church, there is a lighthouse. A very sturdy castle was built around the hill. This is a Portuguese-style building in the East. The center of the castle is a storage depot, built near the sea and the river, so as to facilitate maritime communication. With this as the center, there are six bastions for protection. The remains of one of the bastions were recently discovered at the HSBC Bank site. The Historical Society is now excavating on the hillside opposite the HSBC Bank, looking for the original site of the Portuguese-era buildings. It has now been confirmed that the seawater could reach directly under the city in the past. The changes of the land and sea are truly overwhelming! Looking out from the top of the hill, one can vaguely imagine the scene at that time, with willows shading the houses and water surrounding the city.

On the small hill in front of the government office, a tree called the Malacca tree is specially planted. It was originally very abundant in this area, but it has been almost completely cut down in recent years. Therefore, it is specially planted as a memorial. There is an interesting legend about this tree: it is said that when the nobleman Parameswara was hunting on the beach, his hunting dog chased a deer, but was chased into the sea by the deer instead. The king exclaimed, "This is truly a blessed land, even the deer are brave!" So he built a capital here and named the new capital after the Malacca tree where he rested.

Coming down from St. Paul's Hill, along Ford Road by the sea, there is a long bridge over the sea. Not far away, you will see a city gate made of red clay bricks, standing alone, with towering ancient trees. This is a popular place for locals to take a leisurely stroll after work. It is especially pleasant to stroll here when the sun sets, especially when the Golden Shower Trees are in full bloom, with yellow flowers covering the ground. Enjoying the cool breeze and reciting poetry, the hard work of the day is completely washed away.

"San Bao Hill" is the source of drinking water for this area. There are many wells nearby, all named "San Bao Wells." According to legend, Zheng He once came here, and these wells were all dug by Zheng He. However, this may just be a legend. San Bao Hill is not very high, and there are many mounds of abandoned graves on the hillside. The mountain road is also very rugged and difficult to walk. There is a weather station on the top of the hill, with a panoramic view of the entire slope. Facing the sea in the front, the harbor is clearly visible. Behind it, the green mountains stand opposite St. Paul's Hill and St. John's Hill, with smoke from cooking fires visible in the distance and the sounds of chickens and dogs audible. The beautiful scenery weaves together this beautiful "Ancient Coconut City."

Movie News

Me and Meisheng

— Zhao Dan

On the screen, the roles I play are often very sentimental.

In "Night Fragrance", I still played such a neurotic person; however, it was not the usual intellectual, but a simple-minded farm boy.

"Night Fragrance" is a love tragedy. What is depicted in this film, just like its name, has many sensual elements. The protagonists of the tragedy are a flower girl, A Xiang (played by Hu Die), and Meisheng, the boy I played. Meisheng is in love with A Xiang, but another village girl, A Jin (played by Shu Xiuwen), is in love with Meisheng. Later, A Xiang is taken away by a rich young master from Shanghai (played by Sun Min). Meisheng loses his love and eventually marries A Jin unhappily. But in the end, Meisheng still sacrifices himself for A Xiang.

Young people like Meisheng are naturally not role models. But when I played this role, I was deeply moved by this pitiful young man. Because what this role expresses is not only the bitterness of punished love, but a strong taste of life's bitterness; hidden behind this uneven love tragedy in the golden society is a serious social problem.

I think: if the Meisheng on the screen is not played too badly by me, perhaps he will get some sympathy from the audience?

Picking Up Fragments of Xi Shi

— More

At 9 AM on the 22nd, the Shanghai Theater held a trial performance of the musical drama Xi Shi at the Carlton.

The play is divided into five acts, with four newly made sets (acts four and five share the same set), all of which are extremely luxurious.

Mr. Chen Dabe, the general director, came to the stage twice to deliver "nonsense". Because the reporter was sitting too far away, he couldn't hear very clearly. He probably said that some people criticized the previous "Modern Lady" as a "civilized drama". What is the reason? Because there is no singing and no dancing, the current "Xi Shi" can be called a "barbaric drama".

Yes, "Xi Shi" is quite lively: there are solos, choruses, male dances, and female dances, thanks to the efforts of Mr. Chen Gexin and Mr. Wu Xiaobang.

But in addition to the first scene where Gou Jian sees the King of Wu, the drama has a strong Peking Opera flavor, such as the dialogue and actions (the costumes are ancient costumes, so there is no fault to be found). Someone suggested that if the Qilin Child of the Mountains played Gou Jian first and then Wu Yuan, it would be even more "wonderful", but this is a joke.

In the last scene, Gou Jian and others shouted to the sky on the Gusu Terrace: "Xi Shi's soul is immortal forever!" which received a lot of applause.

Is "Xi Shi" a success?

The play will be performed publicly at the Carlton on the 6th. Please convey Mr. Chen's "nonsense" and ask everyone to introduce more friends and relatives.

Shanghai Daily Building Journal

The Future of Model Villages

— Xiao Ang

In recent years, there has been a new trend and new development in the construction industry, which is the design and construction of model villages. The origin of this new undertaking started in Shanghai because it meets the needs of the Chinese people, especially the people in the cities, so in less than one or two years, this new type of building has sprung up like mushrooms. Now, in Nanjing, Beiping, Tianjin, Guangzhou, Hankou, Qingdao, and other relatively prosperous places, model villages are appearing. Indeed, this is the best phenomenon in China and the best opportunity for the construction industry. However, when it comes to its design, it is inevitably too westernized. China has its own system, and the people have traditional habits. If we imitate all the Western methods, the result will not be good. I have visited several model new villages in Shanghai. The buildings can be said to be magnificent, and the air can be said to be fresh. These are all aristocratic residences and are not what ordinary people need. Therefore, I will also talk about the future of model villages and the future of model villages that the Chinese people need.

(1) General Design

Chinese people have a bad habit, which is that they have no sense of unity, like loose sand. The design of model villages should use the connection of buildings to make the people living in the same village have a mutual loving relationship, and then gradually unite them. The Baojia system currently implemented by the Chinese government is the best way. The design of the model village should take one Jia (that is, ten families) as a small unit, and one Bao (that is, one hundred families) as a village. The residences of the ten families should be built in one place, and there should also be a small office, with the Jia chief's office, public entertainment places, and other Jia's residences designed in the same way. Then, in a suitable place, build a Bao chief's office, which includes the Bao chief's office, a public assembly hall, and a public hospital that can also be attached. If there are many children attending school, a primary school can also be established. In this way, the people living in the same village will definitely have many opportunities to contact each other, and naturally they will become more intimate day by day and united year by year.

(2) Selection of Location

The selection of the location is the most important issue, because the people living in the village are not the capitalist class, but the middle and lower classes of people. They rarely have their own cars and motorcycles, but they have to go to work every day, going out early and returning late. The means of transportation they use are of course buses and trams. The location of the new village should be in a place with convenient transportation. In Shanghai, where transportation is too convenient, the land price must be very expensive, and the air may not be fresh. Therefore, the area around Great Western Road, Zhongshan Road, and Jiangwan's Municipal Government Road in western Shanghai is the best. Another thing to pay attention to is that there should be small towns nearby so that daily necessities and food can be purchased at will. Within one kilometer, there should be small and large factories, because many women can also work during the day to maintain their livelihoods. The problems of electricity and tap water should also be considered. If there is no electricity, it will of course be inconvenient. If the tap water plant cannot supply drinking water for various reasons, it will be a very serious problem, because unclean beverages will affect hygiene, which will run counter to the purpose of building a new village.

(3) Design of Buildings

The residences of model villages are based on small families as units, so a one-story house with a foundation is enough. One living room, and of course the dining room, two bedrooms, one laundry room, and one kitchen. Its floor area is no more than 16x40. The color of the bricks is best to be peach red and yellow because when the sun comes out in the morning, the color of the house is very energetic and can also lift the spirits of some people. Windows and doors are best to face east and south. These are all shallow and easy-to-see things, but it is also worth studying their principles and laws. Flowers and trees should be widely planted around the buildings. Peach and willow are the most suitable for spring scenery, osmanthus and maple trees are the highlights of autumn, and bamboo and pine are the best in winter. The sports field should also be well designed. Tennis is the most suitable for amateur sports, and a small ball field for children is absolutely essential.

The Newest Composition of Residences (Part 1)

— Written by Kenichiichi Shiura, Translated by Zhang Huangzheng

(1) The Function of Residences

It is commonly known that residences occupy the most important position in architecture. To express the essence of residences with more precise wording, it is what the famous French architect Le Corbusier called "a house is a machine for living in." The meaning of this sentence is by no means to say that residences must be built mechanically. Its meaning is simply that the purpose of the creation of residences, in any case, is for habitation.

In short, when residences initially arose as the origin of architecture, their primary purpose was to avoid the threats of nature. Today, this point is still the main purpose, but with the addition of durability requirements, residences have become more developed. Resisting the threats of nature such as rain, snow, cold, heat, earthquakes, floods, fire prevention, and moisture resistance is therefore of great concern to people. From this perspective, if one wants the human life inside the residential house to be comfortable, then the house must have a complete structure.

However, because the residence is entirely a machine for living in, simply having a perfect structure is not fully satisfactory. The design and assembly aspects of a machine are as important as making the machine sturdily with excellent materials. Therefore, in general architecture, it is necessary to know that the design of the layout and various equipment are as important as the structure. In particular, residences, which are most closely related to life, must be engaged in the design of overall control.

(2) The Structure of Residences

Below, I intend to explore these specific issues. However, for the sake of simplicity and clarity, I will only discuss structure and equipment. In general architectural structures, the main thing is to pile up bricks and tiles to make walls, erect beams on pillars, and lay floors below. This type of structure has mechanical differences from wood or steel-reinforced concrete construction.

However, today, in order to adapt to modern life, a more complete structure is inevitably required. Research in this area is very important. At the very least, it must be able to achieve satisfactory effects on the functions of waterproofing, heat prevention, fire prevention, moisture prevention, and soundproofing. However, at the same time, attention must be paid to durability, ease of repair and transformation, and low prices. Of course, it is unreasonable and impossible to seek one or two materials that can meet all these requirements. Therefore, multiple materials must be used to share these responsibilities, thereby creating a well-assembled building. In this sense, people will inevitably pay attention to industrially produced materials. Due to the shortening of the construction period, the price follows with the cheaper "dry construction." This is the so-called structure in which water is not used at the construction site, but only iron or wooden skeletons are erected to create the building. This style has been used a lot in residences and factories. Needless to say, dry construction methods still have many imperfect shortcomings. Undoubtedly, a more perfect construction method will appear in the future.

(3) The Equipment of Residences

With the structure, it is possible to defend against most of the threats of nature. Primitive residences do not know any means other than structure and do not make demands beyond the level of culture. However, due to the development of general culture, the progress of life, and the progress of science, in addition to promoting the development of the structure itself, various equipment has also been created. Heating methods in cold weather, nighttime lighting, methods of supplying and using fuel power, methods of water supply, methods of waste disposal, etc., make the entire residence a complex machine and organic organization.

Among them, the technology of indoor climate regulation has been particularly developed. Compared to the ancient residences with outside climate = inside climate, modern residences that are gradually estranged from the outside world have winter heating and summer cooling rooms for sanitary facilities. Similar to heating and cooling rooms, the temperature and humidity of the air are freely adjusted by various methods. As for the methods of taking temperature, using charcoal fire is extremely cheap; however, it is not hygienic and has many inconveniences and dangers, and is no longer suitable for the needs of the times. In addition to being relatively simple, gas has the same shortcomings as charcoal fire. Electricity, which can be said to be ideal in terms of hygiene and handling, has the only disadvantage of being very expensive and difficult to popularize. If you want the initial equipment cost to be lower, the cost to be low, comfortable and without danger, then there is only steam or hot water heating. In particular, hot water heating, the temperature will not be too high, and the handling is simple, which is most suitable for residential use. In addition to coal, there is also convenient heavy oil for fuel; moreover, there is also an automatic coal feeder for coal, which can be said to be very simple.

Internal Analysis of Ancient Chinese Architecture (Part 2)

— Zhiyun

(5) Pillars—The pillars used in Chinese architecture are completely different from those of other countries and have their own characteristics. When other countries build houses, they must first build the pillars and then build the roof on top of them. However, when Chinese architecture builds, they first make a frame for the roof and then determine the position of the pillars. The wood used is mostly pine wood. The firmness of the frame and top rafters depends entirely on the force of the pillars standing on the stone steps. However, there are brackets supporting the top rafters. There are many brackets, and they are decorative. Chinese pillars are of unparalleled importance, whether they are temples, archways, palaces, or folk houses. Just as in other styles, the capital is the most important part of the building. Whether the pillars are as free-standing as in palaces or are considered part of the wall, they have no capitals and are directly connected to the top rafters of the rectangular roof that is pressed down vertically. And these pillars and roofs are the main objects of palace-style architecture. The half-burned wall does not have any architectural value.

(6) Carvings—In China, roofs and pillars are the main buildings; and their architecture is mostly brick and stone and wood. As for decoration, glazed tiles are used. In decoration, carvings only occupy a small part. In fact, carvings are the same as other styles. When wall tiles extend in, carvings extend out, wave-shaped, round, square, and carved shapes can be seen on the copper base of wooden pillars, but because there are no capitals, there are no carvings on the pillars. Simple carvings can be found on the brackets supporting the top rafters, but they are only decorated with strange carvings. They are also used on the appendages of inlaid circular halls. However, in halls and pagodas, these reliefs can be found under the specially flipped up eaves of overlapping roofs.

(7) Decoration—Chinese decoration shows a national characteristic. Oriental people all show a natural instinct for color, and Chinese people are certainly no exception. Color scheme forms most of Chinese architecture. The roofs are covered with glittering tiles. Yellow is used for palaces; red is used for officials; blue, green, and purple are used for other sections. The exposed roof ridges are decorated with dark dragons, fish, and all kinds of strange-shaped glazed tiles.

No matter where it is, painting some pictures is considered beautiful. Not to mention that palaces need to be decorated; even the houses where common people live also need to be decorated.

After seeing the construction of a setting in the mainland, you can know the national character of the Chinese people.

Research on Indoor Lighting (Part 1)

— Qin

The coordination of indoor lighting is indeed an extremely important task in architecture. The same house, the same arrangement, if the intensity of the light is different, and the coordination of colors is different, it often changes people's feelings and creates a psychology of joy or disgust. Those who work in it are often prone to laziness or inspire them to work hard due to the stimulation of light. Therefore, all residential rooms, factories, schools, and public gathering places should pay twelve points of attention to the coordination of light.

We should know that the benefits of proper indoor lighting are not shallow. In short, (1) it can reduce eye strain, because too strong or too weak light can cause eye strain and consume people's energy; (2) it can reduce fatigue and mental stimulation, because proper light coordination will naturally make people feel comfortable, and their spirits will be revived; (3) it can reduce the occurrence of accidents, such as in factories, where workers become tired due to excessive mental stimulation, and thus the use of machines is improper, and attention gradually weakens, and disasters are likely to occur; (4) it can enhance people's moral concepts, people must have good thoughts when they are happy, and conversely, they are prone to evil thoughts when they are depressed, so the coordination of light must make people feel happy and enhance their moral concepts; (5) it can increase work efficiency, and the reason is very obvious, nothing more than making people feel at ease and concentrate on their work. However, to seek proper coordination of light, one must have a considerable understanding of optics and psychology, and at the same time, one should have a considerable study of the application of various colors, so as to make the indoor layout and decoration neat and beautiful.

The light required indoors can be divided into ordinary and auxiliary types. Ordinary light should be peaceful and refreshing, making people feel comfortable without strong stimulation. The intensity of the light must vary depending on the application of each room. Auxiliary light can also be called dedicated light, because its application is designed for special working conditions indoors, such as reading, drawing, sewing, or other work. This type of work requires stronger light and clearer vision, so ordinary light is not enough to meet its needs, and additional auxiliary or dedicated lighting equipment is required. In addition, the points to be noted are: (1) extremely strong and dazzling light must be completely avoided, and any direct sunlight, light, and light reflected from polished surfaces must be avoided; (2) use white walls and ceilings and other reflective objects to make the light scattered so as not to be dazzling; (3) the light should have sunlight color or very light blue to protect the eyes. It is best to use milky white lampshades or sandblasted bulbs for stronger light to reduce its irritation; (4) the distribution of light intensity must also be determined according to the color of the object, because the light we see is reflected from the object. If the object is dark in color, it must have stronger light shining on it; conversely, weaker light should be used.
